<div class="post" data-id="8612160104870262359" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
<h2 class="title" itemprop="name">
<a href="https://security.googleblog.com/2021/07/measuring-security-risks-in-open-source.html" itemprop="url" title="Measuring Security Risks in Open Source Software: Scorecards Launches V2 ">
Measuring Security Risks in Open Source Software: Scorecards Launches V2 
</a>
</h2>
<div class="post-header">
<div class="published">
<span class="publishdate" itemprop="datePublished">
July 1, 2021
</span>
</div>
</div>
<div class="post-body">
<div class="post-content" itemprop="articleBody">
<script type="text/template">
                          <span class="byline-author">Posted by Kim Lewandowski, Azeem Shaikh, Laurent Simon, Google Open Source Security Team</span><div><span class="byline-author"><br /></span></div><br />Contributors to the <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard">Scorecards project</a>, an automated security tool that produces a &#8220;risk score&#8221; for open source projects, have accomplished a lot since <a href="https://opensource.googleblog.com/2020/11/security-scorecards-for-open-source.html">our launch last fall.</a> Today, in collaboration  with the <a href="https://openssf.org/">Open Source Security Foundation</a> community, we are announcing <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/releases/tag/v2.0.0">Scorecards v2</a>. We have added new security checks, scaled up the number of projects being scored, and made this data easily accessible for analysis.<br /><br /><br />With so much software today relying on open-source projects, consumers need an easy way to judge whether their dependencies are safe. Scorecards helps reduce the toil and manual effort required to continually evaluate changing packages when maintaining a project&#8217;s supply chain. Consumers can automatically assess the risks that dependencies introduce and use this data to make informed decisions about accepting these risks, evaluating alternative solutions, or working with the maintainers to make improvements.<div><br /></div><br /><h3 style="text-align: left;">Identifying Risks</h3><br />Since last fall, Scorecards&#8217; coverage has grown; we've added several new checks, following the <a href="https://security.googleblog.com/2021/02/know-prevent-fix-framework-for-shifting.html">Know, Prevent, Fix framework</a> proposed by Google earlier this year, to prioritize our additions:<br /><br /><div><b>Malicious contributors</b><br /><br />Contributors with malicious intent or compromised accounts can introduce potential backdoors into code. Code reviews help mitigate against such attacks. With the new <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/checks/checks.md#branch-protection">Branch-Protection</a> check, developers can verify that the project enforces mandatory code review from another developer before code is committed. Currently, this check can only be run by a repository admin due to GitHub API limitations. For a third-party repository, use the less informative <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/checks/checks.md#code-review">Code-Review</a> check instead.<br /><br /></div><div><b>Vulnerable code<br /></b><br />Despite best efforts by developers and peer reviews, vulnerable code can enter source control and remain undetected. That&#8217;s why it's important to enable continuous fuzzing and static code analysis to catch bugs early in the development lifecycle. We have added checks to detect if a project uses <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/checks/checks.md#fuzzing">Fuzzing</a> and <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/checks/checks.md#sast">SAST</a> tools as part of their CI/CD system.<br /><b><br /></b></div><div><b>Build system compromise</b><br /><br />A common CI/CD solution used by GitHub projects is <a href="https://github.com/features/actions">GitHub Actions</a>. A danger with these action workflows is that they may handle untrusted user input. Meaning, an attacker can craft a malicious pull request to gain access to the privileged GitHub token, and with it the ability to <a href="https://www.bleepingcomputer.com/news/security/heres-how-a-researcher-broke-into-microsoft-vs-codes-github/">push malicious code to the repo</a> without review. To mitigate this risk, Scorecard's <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/checks/checks.md#token-permissions">Token-Permissions</a> prevention check now verifies that the GitHub workflows follow the principle of least privilege by making GitHub tokens read-only by default.<br /><br /></div><div><b>Bad dependencies</b><br /><br />Any software is as secure as its weakest dependency. This may sound obvious, but the first step to knowing our dependencies is simply to declare them... and have our dependencies declare them too. Once we have this provenance information, we can assess the risks of our software and mitigate those risks. Unfortunately, there are several widely-used anti-patterns that break this provenance principle. The first of these anti-patterns is checked-in binaries -- as there's no way to easily verify or check the contents of the binary in the project. Scorecards provides <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/checks/checks.md#binary-artifacts">Binary-Artifacts</a> check for testing this.<br /><br /><br />Another anti-pattern is the use of curl | bash in scripts which dynamically pulls dependencies. Cryptographic hashes let us pin our dependencies to a known value: if this value ever changes, the build system will detect it and refuse to build. Pinning dependencies is useful everywhere we have dependencies: not just during compilation, but also in Dockerfiles, CI/CD workflows, etc. Scorecards checks for these anti-patterns with the <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/checks/checks.md#frozen-deps">Frozen-Deps</a> check. This check is helpful for mitigating against malicious dependency attacks such as the recent <a href="https://about.codecov.io/security-update/">CodeCov</a> attack.<br /><br /><br />Even with hash-pinning, hashes need to be updated once in a while when dependencies patch vulnerabilities. Tools like <a href="https://docs.github.com/en/code-security/supply-chain-security/managing-vulnerabilities-in-your-projects-dependencies/configuring-dependabot-security-updates">dependabot</a> or <a href="https://github.com/renovatebot/renovate">renovatebot</a> give us the opportunity to review and update the hashes. The Scorecards <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/checks/checks.md#automatic-dependency-update">Automated-Dependency-Update</a> check verifies that developers rely on such tools to update their dependencies.<br /><br /><br />It is important to know vulnerabilities in a project before uptaking it as a dependency. Scorecards can provide this information via the new <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/checks/checks.md#vulnerabilities">Vulnerabilities</a> check, without the need to subscribe to a vulnerability alert system.</div><div><br /></div><div><span id="docs-internal-guid-5a5e70ca-7fff-d253-cfe3-6f935c47390e"><br /></span><h3 style="text-align: left;"><span>Scaling the impact</span></h3><span><br />To date, the Scorecards project has scaled up to evaluate security criteria for over <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/cron/data/projects.csv">50,000</a> open source projects. In order to scale this project, we undertook a massive redesign of our architecture and used a PubSub model which achieved horizontal scalability and higher throughput. This fully automated tool periodically evaluates critical open source projects and exposes the Scorecards check information through a <a href="https://console.cloud.google.com/bigquery?p=openssf&amp;page=table&amp;d=scorecardcron&amp;t=scorecard">public BigQuery dataset</a> which is refreshed weekly.</span></div><div><span><br /></span></div><div><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-5m_2mgrQ3mw/YN0HDhdyQcI/AAAAAAAAAVE/GpZWDDE0qq4HlWxQH5FJ8rrSs-74eBe_QCNcBGAsYHQ/s960/Scorecards%2BUpdate%2BBlog%2BPost_%2BMeasuring%2BSecurity%2BRisk%2Bin%2BOpen%2BSource%2BSoftware.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="720" data-original-width="960" height="300" src="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-5m_2mgrQ3mw/YN0HDhdyQcI/AAAAAAAAAVE/GpZWDDE0qq4HlWxQH5FJ8rrSs-74eBe_QCNcBGAsYHQ/w400-h300/Scorecards%2BUpdate%2BBlog%2BPost_%2BMeasuring%2BSecurity%2BRisk%2Bin%2BOpen%2BSource%2BSoftware.jpg" width="400" /></a></div><br /><span><br /></span></div><div>This data can be retrieved using the <a href="https://cloud.google.com/bigquery/docs/reference/bq-cli-reference">bq command line tool</a>. The following example shows how to export data for the Kubernetes project. Substitute the url for the repo to export data from a different project:</div><div><span><br /><div align="left" dir="ltr" style="margin-left: 0pt;"><table style="border-collapse: collapse; border: none; table-layout: fixed; width: 504pt;"><colgroup><col></col></colgroup><tbody><tr style="height: 0pt;"><td style="border-bottom: solid #000000 1pt; border-left: solid #000000 1pt; border-right: solid #000000 1pt; border-top: solid #000000 1pt; overflow-wrap: break-word; overflow: hidden; padding: 5pt 5pt 5pt 5pt; vertical-align: top;"><p dir="ltr" style="line-height: 1.2; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Courier New&quot;; font-size: 11pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">$ bq query --nouse_legacy_sql 'SELECT Repo, Date, Checks FROM openssf.scorecardcron.scorecard_latest WHERE Repo="github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes"'</span></p></td></tr></tbody></table></div><br />To export the latest data on all analyzed projects, see instructions <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard#public-data">here</a>.<br /></span></div><div><span><br /></span></div><div><h3 style="text-align: left;"><span id="docs-internal-guid-322635e6-7fff-6f46-d4be-a4b9754e61f2">How does the internet measure up?</span></h3><span id="docs-internal-guid-322635e6-7fff-6f46-d4be-a4b9754e61f2">Scorecards data for available projects is now included in the recently <a href="https://opensource.googleblog.com/2021/06/introducing-open-source-insights-project.html">announced</a> Google Open Source Insights <a href="https://deps.dev/">project</a> and also showcased in <a href="http://metrics.openssf.org/">OpenSSF Security Metrics project</a>. The data on these sites shows that there are still important security gaps to fill, even in widely used packages <a href="https://deps.dev/go/k8s.io%2Fkubernetes">like Kubernetes</a>.<br /><br /><br />We also analyzed Scorecards data through Google Data Studio -- one of our data analysis and visualization tools.The diagram below shows a breakdown of the checks that were run and the pass/fail outcome for the 50,000 repositories:<p dir="ltr" style="line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;"><span style="font-family: Arial; font-size: 11pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: Arial; font-size: 11pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;"><span style="border: none; display: inline-block; height: 475px; overflow: hidden; width: 672px;"><img height="475" src="https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/r7BqFbpKExRNXQAiQZQEjve_S7Q670qmOb_7zeEdv2QUfHo6CJBZb6XYtB2zM96Zwv-bmIoU2O6KZeFxR7crYr5-Lc5fu0vpTcUYptuHQ_-Ikhy2OlaJNrwYJX62hfb6pBmTktn9DQjjJVWVmzIavTje13QWNM-GkusjXGehnek9_HQs" style="margin-left: 0px; margin-top: 0px;" width="672" /></span></span></p><br /><br />As we can see, a lot needs to be done to improve the security of these critical projects. A large number of these projects are not continuously <a href="https://github.com/google/oss-fuzz">fuzzed</a>, do not define a security policy for reporting vulnerabilities, and do not pin dependencies, to name just a few common problems. We all need to come together as an industry to drive awareness of these widespread security risks, and to make improvements that will benefit everyone. <br /></span></div><div><br /></div><div><h3 style="text-align: left;"><span>Scorecards in Action</span></h3><span>Several large projects have adopted Scorecards and are keeping us updated on their experiences with it. Below are some examples of Scorecards in action:<br /><b><br /></b></span></div><div><span><b>Envoy</b><br />Early on we <a href="https://blog.envoyproxy.io/security-scorecards-envoy-automating-supply-chain-analysis-7b8fd9829169">talked</a> about how the Envoy maintainers adopted Scorecards for their project and integrated it within their policy on introducing new dependencies. Since then, pull requests introducing new dependencies to Envoy must get approval from a dependency maintainer who uses Scorecards to <a href="https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/DEPENDENCY_POLICY.md#new-external-dependencies">evaluate</a> the dependency against a set of criteria.  <br /><br />In addition, Envoy also got right to work in improving its own security health metrics according to its own Scorecards evaluation, and is now pinning C++ dependencies and <a href="https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/12951">requiring</a> pip hashes for python dependencies. <a href="https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/16579">Github actions</a> are also pinned in the continuous integration flow.<br /><br />Previously, Envoy had created a <a href="https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/tools/dependency/ossf_scorecard.py">tool</a> that outputs Scorecards data on its dependencies as a CSV that can be used to generate a table of results:<br /><p dir="ltr" style="line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt; text-align: center;"><span style="font-family: Arial; font-size: 11pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;"><span style="border: none; display: inline-block; height: 250px; overflow: hidden; width: 486px;"><img height="310.1987210556763" src="https://lh4.googleusercontent.com/YqcstmQ3VDTxdiBJ7kYPWQb9McOreST9vD5g3eb_5FVuUAZTy4JwfES1T0boins0JfTiAeB1mHUNkW35hHJ_qVbJbCETXMkb3heYTWyvatxnkMGExmc0HDTnoe1kEjIbkOHpWH7W3I-lH7FpchKe2B924zsmvvJw-PbVVrpjeMvawwiu" style="margin-left: 0px; margin-top: 0px;" width="486" /></span></span></p><br /><br /></span></div><div><span>Now with more project data, Envoy is able to automatically generate up-to-date Scorecard information about its dependencies and publish it in <a href="https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/intro/arch_overview/security/external_deps">documentation</a>, like the following:</span></div><div><br /><span><p dir="ltr" style="line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;"><span style="font-family: Arial; font-size: 11pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; font-weight: 700; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;"><span style="border: none; display: inline-block; height: 324px; overflow: hidden; width: 672px;"><img height="324" src="https://lh4.googleusercontent.com/tY8dmWzP8B4uNp7M7QuVpeeJ_Baej0oeFvJ9zZ1w4DOvFxdLZOO1WCWWiy-0Lh_3HMFNOwPrNeC5PKjGrer1rFi7XidXiKy_IY7U-hogQys-LSO-BV8g51hxOISKUtNq5iBUMmu8FONWjyQuA1eSmH-j1jSaanrBHDZQpMTes3RLpE4m" style="margin-left: 0px; margin-top: 0px;" width="672" /></span></span></p><br /><b>Scorecards</b><br />We improved our own score for the Scorecards! For example, we are now pinning our own dependencies by hash (e.g. <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/commit/3b1c9b8496a7ff8dad8506691fa28f2d60b14a90">docker dependencies</a>, <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/commit/6367cc44f6a1d8318e452761253f2935b1becd4a">workflow dependencies</a>) to prevent <a href="https://about.codecov.io/security-update/">CodeCov</a> style attacks. We&#8217;ve also included a <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/SECURITY.md">Security Policy</a> based on this <a href="https://github.com/google/oss-vulnerability-guide">recommended template</a>.<div><span style="font-family: Arial; font-size: 11pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;"><br /></span></div></span><h3 style="text-align: left;"><span>Get involved</span></h3><span>We look forward to continuing to grow the Scorecards community. The project now has contributions from <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/graphs/contributors">23</a> developers. Thank you to <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/commits?author=azeemshaikh38">Azeem</a>, <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/commits?author=naveensrinivasan">Naveen</a>, <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/commits?author=laurentsimon">Laurent</a>, <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/commits?author=asraa">Asra</a> and <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/commits?author=chrismcgehee">Chris</a> for their work building these new features and scaling Scorecards. <br /><br />If you would like to join the fun, check out these good first timer <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/issues">issues</a>. <br /><br />If you would like us to help you run Scorecards on specific projects, please submit a GitHub pull request to add those projects <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/cron/data/projects.csv">here</a>.<br /><br />Last but not least, we have a lot of ideas and <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/issues?q=is%3Aopen+is%3Aissue+%22new+check%3A%22">many more checks we&#8217;d like to add</a>, but we want to hear from you. Tell us which checks you would like to see in the next version of Scorecards.</span><h3 style="text-align: left;"><span><br /></span></h3><h3 style="text-align: left;"><span>What&#8217;s next?</span><span><br /></span></h3><span>There are a couple of big enhancements we&#8217;re especially excited about:<br /><br /><ul style="text-align: left;"><li><span><a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/issues/271">Scorecards Badges</a> - GitHub badges to show off compliance</span></li><li><span><a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/issues/193">Integration with CI/CD and GitHub Code Scanning Results</a></span></li><li><span><a href="https://github.com/ossf/allstar">Integration with Allstar project</a> - GitHub App for enforcing security policies</span></li></ul><br />Thanks again to the entire Scorecards community and the OpenSSF for making this project successful. If you&#8217;re adopting and improving the score of the projects you maintain, <a href="https://slack.openssf.org/#security_scorecards">tell us</a> about it. Until next time, keep on improving those scores!</span></div>

<noscript>
<span class="byline-author">Posted by Kim Lewandowski, Azeem Shaikh, Laurent Simon, Google Open Source Security Team</span><div><span class="byline-author"><br/></span></div><br/>Contributors to the <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard">Scorecards project</a>, an automated security tool that produces a “risk score” for open source projects, have accomplished a lot since <a href="https://opensource.googleblog.com/2020/11/security-scorecards-for-open-source.html">our launch last fall.</a> Today, in collaboration  with the <a href="https://openssf.org/">Open Source Security Foundation</a> community, we are announcing <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/releases/tag/v2.0.0">Scorecards v2</a>. We have added new security checks, scaled up the number of projects being scored, and made this data easily accessible for analysis.<br/><br/><br/>With so much software today relying on open-source projects, consumers need an easy way to judge whether their dependencies are safe. Scorecards helps reduce the toil and manual effort required to continually evaluate changing packages when maintaining a project’s supply chain. Consumers can automatically assess the risks that dependencies introduce and use this data to make informed decisions about accepting these risks, evaluating alternative solutions, or working with the maintainers to make improvements.<div><br/></div><br/><h3 style="text-align: left;">Identifying Risks</h3><br/>Since last fall, Scorecards’ coverage has grown; we've added several new checks, following the <a href="https://security.googleblog.com/2021/02/know-prevent-fix-framework-for-shifting.html">Know, Prevent, Fix framework</a> proposed by Google earlier this year, to prioritize our additions:<br/><br/><div><b>Malicious contributors</b><br/><br/>Contributors with malicious intent or compromised accounts can introduce potential backdoors into code. Code reviews help mitigate against such attacks. With the new <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/checks/checks.md#branch-protection">Branch-Protection</a> check, developers can verify that the project enforces mandatory code review from another developer before code is committed. Currently, this check can only be run by a repository admin due to GitHub API limitations. For a third-party repository, use the less informative <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/checks/checks.md#code-review">Code-Review</a> check instead.<br/><br/></div><div><b>Vulnerable code<br/></b><br/>Despite best efforts by developers and peer reviews, vulnerable code can enter source control and remain undetected. That’s why it's important to enable continuous fuzzing and static code analysis to catch bugs early in the development lifecycle. We have added checks to detect if a project uses <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/checks/checks.md#fuzzing">Fuzzing</a> and <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/checks/checks.md#sast">SAST</a> tools as part of their CI/CD system.<br/><b><br/></b></div><div><b>Build system compromise</b><br/><br/>A common CI/CD solution used by GitHub projects is <a href="https://github.com/features/actions">GitHub Actions</a>. A danger with these action workflows is that they may handle untrusted user input. Meaning, an attacker can craft a malicious pull request to gain access to the privileged GitHub token, and with it the ability to <a href="https://www.bleepingcomputer.com/news/security/heres-how-a-researcher-broke-into-microsoft-vs-codes-github/">push malicious code to the repo</a> without review. To mitigate this risk, Scorecard's <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/checks/checks.md#token-permissions">Token-Permissions</a> prevention check now verifies that the GitHub workflows follow the principle of least privilege by making GitHub tokens read-only by default.<br/><br/></div><div><b>Bad dependencies</b><br/><br/>Any software is as secure as its weakest dependency. This may sound obvious, but the first step to knowing our dependencies is simply to declare them... and have our dependencies declare them too. Once we have this provenance information, we can assess the risks of our software and mitigate those risks. Unfortunately, there are several widely-used anti-patterns that break this provenance principle. The first of these anti-patterns is checked-in binaries -- as there's no way to easily verify or check the contents of the binary in the project. Scorecards provides <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/checks/checks.md#binary-artifacts">Binary-Artifacts</a> check for testing this.<br/><br/><br/>Another anti-pattern is the use of curl | bash in scripts which dynamically pulls dependencies. Cryptographic hashes let us pin our dependencies to a known value: if this value ever changes, the build system will detect it and refuse to build. Pinning dependencies is useful everywhere we have dependencies: not just during compilation, but also in Dockerfiles, CI/CD workflows, etc. Scorecards checks for these anti-patterns with the <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/checks/checks.md#frozen-deps">Frozen-Deps</a> check. This check is helpful for mitigating against malicious dependency attacks such as the recent <a href="https://about.codecov.io/security-update/">CodeCov</a> attack.<br/><br/><br/>Even with hash-pinning, hashes need to be updated once in a while when dependencies patch vulnerabilities. Tools like <a href="https://docs.github.com/en/code-security/supply-chain-security/managing-vulnerabilities-in-your-projects-dependencies/configuring-dependabot-security-updates">dependabot</a> or <a href="https://github.com/renovatebot/renovate">renovatebot</a> give us the opportunity to review and update the hashes. The Scorecards <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/checks/checks.md#automatic-dependency-update">Automated-Dependency-Update</a> check verifies that developers rely on such tools to update their dependencies.<br/><br/><br/>It is important to know vulnerabilities in a project before uptaking it as a dependency. Scorecards can provide this information via the new <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/checks/checks.md#vulnerabilities">Vulnerabilities</a> check, without the need to subscribe to a vulnerability alert system.</div><div><br/></div><div><span id="docs-internal-guid-5a5e70ca-7fff-d253-cfe3-6f935c47390e"><br/></span><h3 style="text-align: left;"><span>Scaling the impact</span></h3><span><br/>To date, the Scorecards project has scaled up to evaluate security criteria for over <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/cron/data/projects.csv">50,000</a> open source projects. In order to scale this project, we undertook a massive redesign of our architecture and used a PubSub model which achieved horizontal scalability and higher throughput. This fully automated tool periodically evaluates critical open source projects and exposes the Scorecards check information through a <a href="https://console.cloud.google.com/bigquery?p=openssf&amp;page=table&amp;d=scorecardcron&amp;t=scorecard">public BigQuery dataset</a> which is refreshed weekly.</span></div><div><span><br/></span></div><div><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-5m_2mgrQ3mw/YN0HDhdyQcI/AAAAAAAAAVE/GpZWDDE0qq4HlWxQH5FJ8rrSs-74eBe_QCNcBGAsYHQ/s960/Scorecards%2BUpdate%2BBlog%2BPost_%2BMeasuring%2BSecurity%2BRisk%2Bin%2BOpen%2BSource%2BSoftware.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="720" data-original-width="960" height="300" src="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-5m_2mgrQ3mw/YN0HDhdyQcI/AAAAAAAAAVE/GpZWDDE0qq4HlWxQH5FJ8rrSs-74eBe_QCNcBGAsYHQ/w400-h300/Scorecards%2BUpdate%2BBlog%2BPost_%2BMeasuring%2BSecurity%2BRisk%2Bin%2BOpen%2BSource%2BSoftware.jpg" width="400"/></a></div><br/><span><br/></span></div><div>This data can be retrieved using the <a href="https://cloud.google.com/bigquery/docs/reference/bq-cli-reference">bq command line tool</a>. The following example shows how to export data for the Kubernetes project. Substitute the url for the repo to export data from a different project:</div><div><span><br/><div align="left" dir="ltr" style="margin-left: 0pt;"><table style="border-collapse: collapse; border: none; table-layout: fixed; width: 504pt;"><colgroup><col/></colgroup><tbody><tr style="height: 0pt;"><td style="border-bottom: solid #000000 1pt; border-left: solid #000000 1pt; border-right: solid #000000 1pt; border-top: solid #000000 1pt; overflow-wrap: break-word; overflow: hidden; padding: 5pt 5pt 5pt 5pt; vertical-align: top;"><p dir="ltr" style="line-height: 1.2; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;"><span style='font-family: "Courier New"; font-size: 11pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;'>$ bq query --nouse_legacy_sql 'SELECT Repo, Date, Checks FROM openssf.scorecardcron.scorecard_latest WHERE Repo="github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes"'</span></p></td></tr></tbody></table></div><br/>To export the latest data on all analyzed projects, see instructions <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard#public-data">here</a>.<br/></span></div><div><span><br/></span></div><div><h3 style="text-align: left;"><span id="docs-internal-guid-322635e6-7fff-6f46-d4be-a4b9754e61f2">How does the internet measure up?</span></h3><span id="docs-internal-guid-322635e6-7fff-6f46-d4be-a4b9754e61f2">Scorecards data for available projects is now included in the recently <a href="https://opensource.googleblog.com/2021/06/introducing-open-source-insights-project.html">announced</a> Google Open Source Insights <a href="https://deps.dev/">project</a> and also showcased in <a href="http://metrics.openssf.org/">OpenSSF Security Metrics project</a>. The data on these sites shows that there are still important security gaps to fill, even in widely used packages <a href="https://deps.dev/go/k8s.io%2Fkubernetes">like Kubernetes</a>.<br/><br/><br/>We also analyzed Scorecards data through Google Data Studio -- one of our data analysis and visualization tools.The diagram below shows a breakdown of the checks that were run and the pass/fail outcome for the 50,000 repositories:<p dir="ltr" style="line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;"><span style="font-family: Arial; font-size: 11pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;"> </span><span style="font-family: Arial; font-size: 11pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;"><span style="border: none; display: inline-block; height: 475px; overflow: hidden; width: 672px;"><img height="475" src="https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/r7BqFbpKExRNXQAiQZQEjve_S7Q670qmOb_7zeEdv2QUfHo6CJBZb6XYtB2zM96Zwv-bmIoU2O6KZeFxR7crYr5-Lc5fu0vpTcUYptuHQ_-Ikhy2OlaJNrwYJX62hfb6pBmTktn9DQjjJVWVmzIavTje13QWNM-GkusjXGehnek9_HQs" style="margin-left: 0px; margin-top: 0px;" width="672"/></span></span></p><br/><br/>As we can see, a lot needs to be done to improve the security of these critical projects. A large number of these projects are not continuously <a href="https://github.com/google/oss-fuzz">fuzzed</a>, do not define a security policy for reporting vulnerabilities, and do not pin dependencies, to name just a few common problems. We all need to come together as an industry to drive awareness of these widespread security risks, and to make improvements that will benefit everyone. <br/></span></div><div><br/></div><div><h3 style="text-align: left;"><span>Scorecards in Action</span></h3><span>Several large projects have adopted Scorecards and are keeping us updated on their experiences with it. Below are some examples of Scorecards in action:<br/><b><br/></b></span></div><div><span><b>Envoy</b><br/>Early on we <a href="https://blog.envoyproxy.io/security-scorecards-envoy-automating-supply-chain-analysis-7b8fd9829169">talked</a> about how the Envoy maintainers adopted Scorecards for their project and integrated it within their policy on introducing new dependencies. Since then, pull requests introducing new dependencies to Envoy must get approval from a dependency maintainer who uses Scorecards to <a href="https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/DEPENDENCY_POLICY.md#new-external-dependencies">evaluate</a> the dependency against a set of criteria.  <br/><br/>In addition, Envoy also got right to work in improving its own security health metrics according to its own Scorecards evaluation, and is now pinning C++ dependencies and <a href="https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/12951">requiring</a> pip hashes for python dependencies. <a href="https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/16579">Github actions</a> are also pinned in the continuous integration flow.<br/><br/>Previously, Envoy had created a <a href="https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/tools/dependency/ossf_scorecard.py">tool</a> that outputs Scorecards data on its dependencies as a CSV that can be used to generate a table of results:<br/><p dir="ltr" style="line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt; text-align: center;"><span style="font-family: Arial; font-size: 11pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;"><span style="border: none; display: inline-block; height: 250px; overflow: hidden; width: 486px;"><img height="310.1987210556763" src="https://lh4.googleusercontent.com/YqcstmQ3VDTxdiBJ7kYPWQb9McOreST9vD5g3eb_5FVuUAZTy4JwfES1T0boins0JfTiAeB1mHUNkW35hHJ_qVbJbCETXMkb3heYTWyvatxnkMGExmc0HDTnoe1kEjIbkOHpWH7W3I-lH7FpchKe2B924zsmvvJw-PbVVrpjeMvawwiu" style="margin-left: 0px; margin-top: 0px;" width="486"/></span></span></p><br/><br/></span></div><div><span>Now with more project data, Envoy is able to automatically generate up-to-date Scorecard information about its dependencies and publish it in <a href="https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/intro/arch_overview/security/external_deps">documentation</a>, like the following:</span></div><div><br/><span><p dir="ltr" style="line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;"><span style="font-family: Arial; font-size: 11pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; font-weight: 700; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;"><span style="border: none; display: inline-block; height: 324px; overflow: hidden; width: 672px;"><img height="324" src="https://lh4.googleusercontent.com/tY8dmWzP8B4uNp7M7QuVpeeJ_Baej0oeFvJ9zZ1w4DOvFxdLZOO1WCWWiy-0Lh_3HMFNOwPrNeC5PKjGrer1rFi7XidXiKy_IY7U-hogQys-LSO-BV8g51hxOISKUtNq5iBUMmu8FONWjyQuA1eSmH-j1jSaanrBHDZQpMTes3RLpE4m" style="margin-left: 0px; margin-top: 0px;" width="672"/></span></span></p><br/><b>Scorecards</b><br/>We improved our own score for the Scorecards! For example, we are now pinning our own dependencies by hash (e.g. <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/commit/3b1c9b8496a7ff8dad8506691fa28f2d60b14a90">docker dependencies</a>, <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/commit/6367cc44f6a1d8318e452761253f2935b1becd4a">workflow dependencies</a>) to prevent <a href="https://about.codecov.io/security-update/">CodeCov</a> style attacks. We’ve also included a <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/SECURITY.md">Security Policy</a> based on this <a href="https://github.com/google/oss-vulnerability-guide">recommended template</a>.<div><span style="font-family: Arial; font-size: 11pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;"><br/></span></div></span><h3 style="text-align: left;"><span>Get involved</span></h3><span>We look forward to continuing to grow the Scorecards community. The project now has contributions from <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/graphs/contributors">23</a> developers. Thank you to <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/commits?author=azeemshaikh38">Azeem</a>, <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/commits?author=naveensrinivasan">Naveen</a>, <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/commits?author=laurentsimon">Laurent</a>, <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/commits?author=asraa">Asra</a> and <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/commits?author=chrismcgehee">Chris</a> for their work building these new features and scaling Scorecards. <br/><br/>If you would like to join the fun, check out these good first timer <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/issues">issues</a>. <br/><br/>If you would like us to help you run Scorecards on specific projects, please submit a GitHub pull request to add those projects <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/blob/main/cron/data/projects.csv">here</a>.<br/><br/>Last but not least, we have a lot of ideas and <a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/issues?q=is%3Aopen+is%3Aissue+%22new+check%3A%22">many more checks we’d like to add</a>, but we want to hear from you. Tell us which checks you would like to see in the next version of Scorecards.</span><h3 style="text-align: left;"><span><br/></span></h3><h3 style="text-align: left;"><span>What’s next?</span><span><br/></span></h3><span>There are a couple of big enhancements we’re especially excited about:<br/><br/><ul style="text-align: left;"><li><span><a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/issues/271">Scorecards Badges</a> - GitHub badges to show off compliance</span></li><li><span><a href="https://github.com/ossf/scorecard/issues/193">Integration with CI/CD and GitHub Code Scanning Results</a></span></li><li><span><a href="https://github.com/ossf/allstar">Integration with Allstar project</a> - GitHub App for enforcing security policies</span></li></ul><br/>Thanks again to the entire Scorecards community and the OpenSSF for making this project successful. If you’re adopting and improving the score of the projects you maintain, <a href="https://slack.openssf.org/#security_scorecards">tell us</a> about it. Until next time, keep on improving those scores!</span></div>

<div class="post" data-id="4834442289702846747" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
<h2 class="title" itemprop="name">
<a href="https://security.googleblog.com/2021/06/announcing-unified-vulnerability-schema.html" itemprop="url" title="Announcing a unified vulnerability schema for open source">
Announcing a unified vulnerability schema for open source
</a>
</h2>
<div class="post-header">
<div class="published">
<span class="publishdate" itemprop="datePublished">
June 24, 2021
</span>
</div>
</div>
<div class="post-body">
<div class="post-content" itemprop="articleBody">
<script type="text/template">
                          <h4 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-weight: normal;"><span class="byline-author">Posted by Oliver Chang, Google Open Source Security team and Russ Cox, Go team&nbsp;</span></span></h4><br />In recent months, Google has launched <a href="https://security.googleblog.com/2021/02/know-prevent-fix-framework-for-shifting.html">several efforts</a> to strengthen open-source security on multiple fronts. One important focus is improving how we identify and respond to known security vulnerabilities without doing extensive manual work. It is essential to have a precise common data format to triage and remediate security vulnerabilities, particularly when communicating about risks to affected dependencies&#8212;it enables easier automation and empowers consumers of open-source software to know when they are impacted and make security fixes as soon as possible.<br /><br />We released the <a href="https://opensource.googleblog.com/2021/02/launching-osv-better-vulnerability.html">Open Source Vulnerabilities (OSV) database</a> in February with the goal of automating and improving vulnerability triage for developers and users of open source software. This initial effort was bootstrapped with a dataset of a few thousand vulnerabilities from the <a href="https://github.com/google/oss-fuzz">OSS-Fuzz</a> project. Implementing OSV to communicate precise vulnerability data for hundreds of critical open-source projects proved the success and utility of the format, and garnered feedback to help us improve the project; for example, we dropped the Cloud API key requirement, making the database even easier to access by more users. The community response also showed that there was broad interest in extending the effort further.<br /><br />Today, we&#8217;re excited to announce a new milestone in expanding OSV to several key open-source ecosystems: <a href="https://github.com/golang/vulndb">Go</a>, <a href="https://github.com/RustSec/advisory-db">Rust</a>, <a href="https://github.com/pypa/advisory-db">Python</a>, and <a href="https://github.com/distributedweaknessfiling/dwflist">DWF</a>. This expansion unites and aggregates four important vulnerability databases, giving software developers a better way to track and remediate the security issues that affect them. Our effort also aligns with the recent <a href="https://www.federalregister.gov/documents/2021/05/17/2021-10460/improving-the-nations-cybersecurity">US Executive Order on Improving the Nation&#8217;s Cybersecurity</a>, which emphasized the need to remove barriers to sharing threat information in order to strengthen national infrastructure. This expanded shared vulnerability database marks an important step toward creating a more secure open-source environment for all users.<div>&nbsp; <br /><b>A simple, unified schema for describing vulnerabilities precisely</b><br /><br />As with open source development, vulnerability databases in open source follow a distributed model, with many ecosystems and organizations creating their own database. Since each uses their own format to describe vulnerabilities, a client tracking vulnerabilities across multiple databases must handle each completely separately. Sharing of vulnerabilities between databases is also difficult.<br /><br />The Google Open Source Security team, Go team, and the broader open-source community have been developing a simple <a href="https://tinyurl.com/vuln-json">vulnerability interchange schema</a> for describing vulnerabilities that&#8217;s designed from the beginning for open-source ecosystems. After starting work on the schema a few months ago, we <a href="http://tinyurl.com/vuln-json">requested public feedback and received hundreds of comments</a>. We have incorporated the input from readers to arrive at the current schema:<div><br /><div><span id="docs-internal-guid-ed5a238f-7fff-2b6d-1566-a048811a11fd"><div align="left" dir="ltr" style="margin-left: 0pt;"><table style="border-collapse: collapse; border: none;"><colgroup></colgroup><tbody><tr style="height: 0pt;"><td style="background-color: #fafafa; border-bottom: solid #e0e0e0 1pt; border-color: rgb(224, 224, 224); border-left: solid #e0e0e0 1pt; border-right: solid #e0e0e0 1pt; border-style: solid; border-top: solid #e0e0e0 1pt; border-width: 1pt; overflow-wrap: break-word; overflow: hidden; padding: 5pt; vertical-align: top;"><p dir="ltr" style="line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;"><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">{</span></p><p dir="ltr" style="line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;"><span style="background-color: transparent; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; </span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #0f9d58; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">"id"</span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">:</span><span style="background-color: transparent; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;"> </span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #9c27b0; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">string</span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">,</span></p><p dir="ltr" style="line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;"><span style="background-color: transparent; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; </span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #0f9d58; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">"modified"</span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">:</span><span style="background-color: transparent; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;"> </span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #9c27b0; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">string</span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">,</span></p><p dir="ltr" style="line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;"><span style="background-color: transparent; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; </span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #0f9d58; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">"published"</span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">:</span><span style="background-color: transparent; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;"> </span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #9c27b0; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">string</span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">,</span></p><p dir="ltr" style="line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;"><span style="background-color: transparent; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; </span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #0f9d58; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">"withdrawn"</span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">:</span><span style="background-color: transparent; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;"> </span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #9c27b0; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">string</span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">,</span></p><p dir="ltr" style="line-height: 1.38; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">"versions"</span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">],</span></p><p dir="ltr" style="line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;"><span style="background-color: transparent; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; </span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #0f9d58; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">"ecosystem_specific"</span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">:</span><span style="background-color: transparent; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;"> </span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">{</span><span style="background-color: transparent; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;"> see spec </span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">},</span></p><p dir="ltr" style="line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;"><span style="background-color: transparent; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; </span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #0f9d58; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">"database_specific"</span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">:</span><span style="background-color: transparent; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;"> </span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">{</span><span style="background-color: transparent; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;"> see spec </span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">},</span></p><p dir="ltr" style="line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;"><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">}</span></p></td></tr></tbody></table><br /></div><br />This new vulnerability schema aims to address some key problems with managing vulnerabilities in open source. We found that there was no existing standard format which: <br /><br /><ul style="text-align: left;"><li><span id="docs-internal-guid-ed5a238f-7fff-2b6d-1566-a048811a11fd">Enforces version specification that precisely matches naming and versioning schemes used in actual open source package ecosystems. For instance, matching a vulnerability such as a <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/">CVE</a> to a package name and set of versions in a package manager is difficult to do in an automated way using existing mechanisms such as <a href="https://nvd.nist.gov/products/cpe">CPEs</a>.</span></li><li><span id="docs-internal-guid-ed5a238f-7fff-2b6d-1566-a048811a11fd">Can be used to describe vulnerabilities in any open source ecosystem, while not requiring ecosystem-dependent logic to process them.</span></li><li><span id="docs-internal-guid-ed5a238f-7fff-2b6d-1566-a048811a11fd">Is easy to use by both automated systems and humans.</span></li></ul><br />With this schema we hope to define a format that all vulnerability databases can export. A unified format means that vulnerability databases, open source users, and security researchers can easily share tooling and consume vulnerabilities across all of open source. This means a more complete view of vulnerabilities in open source for everyone, as well as faster detection and remediation times resulting from easier automation.<br /></span></div><div><br /></div><h2 style="text-align: left;">The current state</h2><div><span><br /></span></div><div><span>The <a href="https://tinyurl.com/vuln-json">vulnerability schema spec</a> has gone through several iterations, and we are inviting further feedback as it gets closer to finalized. A number of public vulnerability databases today are already exporting this format, with more in the pipeline:<br /><ul style="text-align: left;"><li><span><a href="https://github.com/golang/vulndb">Go vulnerability database</a> for Go packages</span></li><li><span><a href="https://github.com/RustSec/advisory-db">Rust advisory database</a> for Cargo packages</span></li><li><span><a href="https://github.com/pypa/advisory-db">Python advisory database</a> for PyPI packages</span></li><li><span><a href="https://github.com/distributedweaknessfiling/dwflist">DWF database</a> for vulnerabilities in the Linux kernel and other popular software</span></li><li><span><a href="https://github.com/google/oss-fuzz-vulns">OSS-Fuzz database</a> for vulnerabilities in C/C++ software found by OSS-Fuzz</span></li></ul>The OSV service has also aggregated all of these vulnerability databases, which are viewable at our <a href="https://osv.dev/list">web UI</a>. They can also be queried with a single command via the same <a href="https://osv.dev/docs/#tag/api">existing APIs</a>:</span></div></div><div><span><br /></span></div><div><span id="docs-internal-guid-1ad18e4a-7fff-cbb7-67da-ef7557fa3f5f"><div align="left" dir="ltr" style="margin-left: 0pt;"><table style="border-collapse: collapse; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span style="background-color: transparent; color: #0f9d58; font-family: &quot;Roboto Mono&quot;, monospace; font-size: 9pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;">"https://api.osv.dev/v1/query"</span></p></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div><span><br /></span></div><br /></span><h2 style="text-align: left;"><span>Automating vulnerability database maintenance</span></h2><span><div><span><br /></span></div>Producing quality vulnerability data is also difficult. In addition to <a href="https://opensource.googleblog.com/2021/02/launching-osv-better-vulnerability.html">OSV&#8217;s existing automation</a>, we built more <a href="https://github.com/google/osv/tree/master/vulnfeeds">automation tools</a> for vulnerability database maintenance, and used these tools to <a href="https://discuss.python.org/t/proposing-a-community-maintained-database-of-pypi-package-vulnerabilities/8374/13">bootstrap</a> the community <a href="https://github.com/pypa/advisory-db">Python advisory database</a>. This automation takes existing feeds, accurately matches them to packages, and <a href="https://github.com/pypa/advisory-db/commit/7afe2510b693ad60a0b95da8a5b2a370a7c48997">generates entries</a> containing <a href="https://github.com/pypa/advisory-db/commit/e4035d8131324cf207ac9b40eacac79b97b1c6b2">precise, validated version ranges</a> with minimal human intervention. We plan to extend this tooling to other ecosystems for which there is no existing vulnerability database, or little support for ongoing database maintenance.<br /></span></div><div><h2 style="text-align: left;"><span><br /></span></h2><h2 style="text-align: left;"><span>Get involved</span></h2><span><div><span><br /></span></div>Thank you to all the open source developers who have provided feedback and adopted this format. We&#8217;re continuing to work with open source communities to develop this further and earn more widespread adoption in all ecosystems. If you are interested in adopting this format, we&#8217;d appreciate any feedback on our <a href="https://tinyurl.com/vuln-json">public spec</a>.<br /></span></div></div>
<span itemprop='author' itemscope='itemscope' itemtype='http://schema.org/Person'>
  <meta content='https://plus.google.com/116899029375914044550' itemprop='url'/>
</span>
                        </script>
<noscript>
<h4 style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-weight: normal;"><span class="byline-author">Posted by Oliver Chang, Google Open Source Security team and Russ Cox, Go team </span></span></h4><br/>In recent months, Google has launched <a href="https://security.googleblog.com/2021/02/know-prevent-fix-framework-for-shifting.html">several efforts</a> to strengthen open-source security on multiple fronts. One important focus is improving how we identify and respond to known security vulnerabilities without doing extensive manual work. It is essential to have a precise common data format to triage and remediate security vulnerabilities, particularly when communicating about risks to affected dependencies—it enables easier automation and empowers consumers of open-source software to know when they are impacted and make security fixes as soon as possible.<br/><br/>We released the <a href="https://opensource.googleblog.com/2021/02/launching-osv-better-vulnerability.html">Open Source Vulnerabilities (OSV) database</a> in February with the goal of automating and improving vulnerability triage for developers and users of open source software. This initial effort was bootstrapped with a dataset of a few thousand vulnerabilities from the <a href="https://github.com/google/oss-fuzz">OSS-Fuzz</a> project. Implementing OSV to communicate precise vulnerability data for hundreds of critical open-source projects proved the success and utility of the format, and garnered feedback to help us improve the project; for example, we dropped the Cloud API key requirement, making the database even easier to access by more users. The community response also showed that there was broad interest in extending the effort further.<br/><br/>Today, we’re excited to announce a new milestone in expanding OSV to several key open-source ecosystems: <a href="https://github.com/golang/vulndb">Go</a>, <a href="https://github.com/RustSec/advisory-db">Rust</a>, <a href="https://github.com/pypa/advisory-db">Python</a>, and <a href="https://github.com/distributedweaknessfiling/dwflist">DWF</a>. This expansion unites and aggregates four important vulnerability databases, giving software developers a better way to track and remediate the security issues that affect them. Our effort also aligns with the recent <a href="https://www.federalregister.gov/documents/2021/05/17/2021-10460/improving-the-nations-cybersecurity">US Executive Order on Improving the Nation’s Cybersecurity</a>, which emphasized the need to remove barriers to sharing threat information in order to strengthen national infrastructure. This expanded shared vulnerability database marks an important step toward creating a more secure open-source environment for all users.<div>  <br/><b>A simple, unified schema for describing vulnerabilities precisely</b><br/><br/>As with open source development, vulnerability databases in open source follow a distributed model, with many ecosystems and organizations creating their own database. Since each uses their own format to describe vulnerabilities, a client tracking vulnerabilities across multiple databases must handle each completely separately. Sharing of vulnerabilities between databases is also difficult.<br/><br/>The Google Open Source Security team, Go team, and the broader open-source community have been developing a simple <a href="https://tinyurl.com/vuln-json">vulnerability interchange schema</a> for describing vulnerabilities that’s designed from the beginning for open-source ecosystems. After starting work on the schema a few months ago, we <a href="http://tinyurl.com/vuln-json">requested public feedback and received hundreds of comments</a>. We have incorporated the input from readers to arrive at the current schema:<div><br/><div><span id="docs-internal-guid-ed5a238f-7fff-2b6d-1566-a048811a11fd"><div align="left" dir="ltr" style="margin-left: 0pt;"><table style="border-collapse: collapse; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;"><span style='background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: "Roboto Mono", monospace; font-size: 10pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;'>}</span></p></td></tr></tbody></table><br/></div><br/>This new vulnerability schema aims to address some key problems with managing vulnerabilities in open source. We found that there was no existing standard format which: <br/><br/><ul style="text-align: left;"><li><span id="docs-internal-guid-ed5a238f-7fff-2b6d-1566-a048811a11fd">Enforces version specification that precisely matches naming and versioning schemes used in actual open source package ecosystems. For instance, matching a vulnerability such as a <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/">CVE</a> to a package name and set of versions in a package manager is difficult to do in an automated way using existing mechanisms such as <a href="https://nvd.nist.gov/products/cpe">CPEs</a>.</span></li><li><span id="docs-internal-guid-ed5a238f-7fff-2b6d-1566-a048811a11fd">Can be used to describe vulnerabilities in any open source ecosystem, while not requiring ecosystem-dependent logic to process them.</span></li><li><span id="docs-internal-guid-ed5a238f-7fff-2b6d-1566-a048811a11fd">Is easy to use by both automated systems and humans.</span></li></ul><br/>With this schema we hope to define a format that all vulnerability databases can export. A unified format means that vulnerability databases, open source users, and security researchers can easily share tooling and consume vulnerabilities across all of open source. This means a more complete view of vulnerabilities in open source for everyone, as well as faster detection and remediation times resulting from easier automation.<br/></span></div><div><br/></div><h2 style="text-align: left;">The current state</h2><div><span><br/></span></div><div><span>The <a href="https://tinyurl.com/vuln-json">vulnerability schema spec</a> has gone through several iterations, and we are inviting further feedback as it gets closer to finalized. A number of public vulnerability databases today are already exporting this format, with more in the pipeline:<br/><ul style="text-align: left;"><li><span><a href="https://github.com/golang/vulndb">Go vulnerability database</a> for Go packages</span></li><li><span><a href="https://github.com/RustSec/advisory-db">Rust advisory database</a> for Cargo packages</span></li><li><span><a href="https://github.com/pypa/advisory-db">Python advisory database</a> for PyPI packages</span></li><li><span><a href="https://github.com/distributedweaknessfiling/dwflist">DWF database</a> for vulnerabilities in the Linux kernel and other popular software</span></li><li><span><a href="https://github.com/google/oss-fuzz-vulns">OSS-Fuzz database</a> for vulnerabilities in C/C++ software found by OSS-Fuzz</span></li></ul>The OSV service has also aggregated all of these vulnerability databases, which are viewable at our <a href="https://osv.dev/list">web UI</a>. They can also be queried with a single command via the same <a href="https://osv.dev/docs/#tag/api">existing APIs</a>:</span></div></div><div><span><br/></span></div><div><span id="docs-internal-guid-1ad18e4a-7fff-cbb7-67da-ef7557fa3f5f"><div align="left" dir="ltr" style="margin-left: 0pt;"><table style="border-collapse: collapse; border: none;"><colgroup></colgroup><tbody><tr style="height: 0pt;"><td style="background-color: #fafafa; border-bottom: solid #e0e0e0 1pt; border-color: rgb(224, 224, 224); border-left: solid #e0e0e0 1pt; border-right: solid #e0e0e0 1pt; border-style: solid; border-top: solid #e0e0e0 1pt; border-width: 1pt; overflow-wrap: break-word; overflow: hidden; padding: 5pt; vertical-align: top;"><p dir="ltr" style="line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;"><span style='background-color: transparent; font-family: "Roboto Mono", monospace; font-size: 9pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;'>  curl </span><span style='background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: "Roboto Mono", monospace; font-size: 9pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;'>-</span><span style='background-color: transparent; font-family: "Roboto Mono", monospace; font-size: 9pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; white-space: pre-wrap;'>      </span><span style='background-color: transparent; color: #0f9d58; font-family: "Roboto Mono", monospace; font-size: 9pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;'>'{"commit": "a46c08c533cfdf10260e74e2c03fa84a13b6c456"}'</span><span style='background-color: transparent; font-family: "Roboto Mono", monospace; font-size: 9pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;'> </span><span style='background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: "Roboto Mono", monospace; font-size: 9pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;'>\</span></p><p dir="ltr" style="line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;"><span style='background-color: transparent; font-family: "Roboto Mono", monospace; font-size: 9pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;'>      </span><span style='background-color: transparent; color: #0f9d58; font-family: "Roboto Mono", monospace; font-size: 9pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;'>"https://api.osv.dev/v1/query"</span></p><p dir="ltr" style="line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;"><span style='background-color: transparent; font-family: "Roboto Mono", monospace; font-size: 9pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;'>    </span></p><p dir="ltr" style="line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;"><span style='background-color: transparent; font-family: "Roboto Mono", monospace; font-size: 9pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;'>  curl </span><span style='background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: "Roboto Mono", monospace; font-size: 9pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;'>-</span><span style='background-color: transparent; font-family: "Roboto Mono", monospace; font-size: 9pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;'>X POST </span><span style='background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: "Roboto Mono", monospace; font-size: 9pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;'>-</span><span style='background-color: transparent; font-family: "Roboto Mono", monospace; font-size: 9pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;'>d </span><span style='background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: "Roboto Mono", monospace; font-size: 9pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;'>\</span></p><p dir="ltr" style="line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;"><span style='background-color: transparent; font-family: "Roboto Mono", monospace; font-size: 9pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;'>      </span><span style='background-color: transparent; color: #0f9d58; font-family: "Roboto Mono", monospace; font-size: 9pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;'>'{"version": "2.4.1", "package": {"name": "jinja2", "ecosystem": "PyPI"}}'</span><span style='background-color: transparent; font-family: "Roboto Mono", monospace; font-size: 9pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;'> </span><span style='background-color: transparent; color: #616161; font-family: "Roboto Mono", monospace; font-size: 9pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;'>\</span></p><p dir="ltr" style="line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;"><span style='background-color: transparent; font-family: "Roboto Mono", monospace; font-size: 9pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;'>      </span><span style='background-color: transparent; color: #0f9d58; font-family: "Roboto Mono", monospace; font-size: 9pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;'>"https://api.osv.dev/v1/query"</span></p></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div><span><br/></span></div><br/></span><h2 style="text-align: left;"><span>Automating vulnerability database maintenance</span></h2><span><div><span><br/></span></div>Producing quality vulnerability data is also difficult. In addition to <a href="https://opensource.googleblog.com/2021/02/launching-osv-better-vulnerability.html">OSV’s existing automation</a>, we built more <a href="https://github.com/google/osv/tree/master/vulnfeeds">automation tools</a> for vulnerability database maintenance, and used these tools to <a href="https://discuss.python.org/t/proposing-a-community-maintained-database-of-pypi-package-vulnerabilities/8374/13">bootstrap</a> the community <a href="https://github.com/pypa/advisory-db">Python advisory database</a>. This automation takes existing feeds, accurately matches them to packages, and <a href="https://github.com/pypa/advisory-db/commit/7afe2510b693ad60a0b95da8a5b2a370a7c48997">generates entries</a> containing <a href="https://github.com/pypa/advisory-db/commit/e4035d8131324cf207ac9b40eacac79b97b1c6b2">precise, validated version ranges</a> with minimal human intervention. We plan to extend this tooling to other ecosystems for which there is no existing vulnerability database, or little support for ongoing database maintenance.<br/></span></div><div><h2 style="text-align: left;"><span><br/></span></h2><h2 style="text-align: left;"><span>Get involved</span></h2><span><div><span><br/></span></div>Thank you to all the open source developers who have provided feedback and adopted this format. We’re continuing to work with open source communities to develop this further and earn more widespread adoption in all ecosystems. If you are interested in adopting this format, we’d appreciate any feedback on our <a href="https://tinyurl.com/vuln-json">public spec</a>.<br/></span></div></div>
<span itemprop="author" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
<meta content="https://plus.google.com/116899029375914044550" itemprop="url"/>
</span>
</noscript>
</div>
</div>

      // Social sharing popups.
      var postEl = document.getElementsByClassName('social-wrapper');
      var postCount = postEl.length;
      for(i=0; i<postCount;i++){
        postEl[i].addEventListener("click", function(event){

          window.open(
